dou derrompement dou ventre	because of the disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The disruptions of the belly are great and frequent and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound often the intestine, or the knots of the intestines, which prevents the intrusion of aus;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more painful, and often it is better to have a small wound than a large one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one puts back together the inner parts, so that they are not repeatedly dislocated.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell so much that they feel cold, if they return to their place,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because it is necessary to soothe the wounded belly, because one must reset the intestine to its place, like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common stitches have an incision in the stitches of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitches for other wounds of the body and these proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and however they are more suitable with the stitches of the belly, and I will describe each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and none of the intestines are outside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and this thing is to reset, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	by the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is frozen, warm it up in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Here is the translation:
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	where you burn with a hot iron and cautery and branding,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and scorch the intestine until the inflammation is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and many times they make these veins retreat, and it is wonderful that one heals by removing the inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the inflammation departing, then anoint the intestine with hot or cold water and evil humors are cured,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this it is aligned the entrance to little of thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little wound at the instrument with which one collects the humors;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to soften what is hardened;
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut without great necessity there is;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and it's the instruments for the wound:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut deeply into the curvature and do not dig further, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you reset it according to its natural shape in its own place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	Here is the translation:
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is on the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	If you set the head and the foot higher than the parts below,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and thus the rupture of the wind in one of the lower parties
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you set it in a way that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus you must minister to what I say about great wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds put this in order that it appears to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then hold it between your hands, I minister piteously which draws the whole route to his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of stitches,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound, an inch of space, and I fix a needle or where it has a strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the skin with the skin of the siphos,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather the nine chief veins which are called siphac; gather them together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then stretch a double thread within the needle of the vein, because
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather the nine heads of the wound healing,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then let the two fingers of space, and fix another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then let the thread of fire thus as you did the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing this according to what you have mastered with the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the needles subtle, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the subtle needles take in all the flesh, and those too large cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for it is necessary that they be blunt;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and soft skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not take in and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the heads of the veins so they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I hold tight or wrap around the heads of the veins to keep them still,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sewn up;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of cutting the veins is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because he suffers from a needle or a puncture wound.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second pain is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you gather the needle-pricked heads of leather and the needle-pricked heads of skin together into a single point or where it has a strong, firm thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these heads all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you reset the needle to the part where you started, in the manner that one cuts the threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a smaller finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch follows the bone,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that one had on their hand or belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a blow
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's breadth large,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was about twenty palms' breadth of intestine,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I will return the intestine, then it has been stopped for 23 hours, forthwith.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up to the 15th day, and it was healed, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not heal at all from the ointment, for I was in a place where none was found, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply a remedy with more pressure on the wound cotton often many times a day, and the washing of honey water as long as it was healing.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and sew the part that is deficient just up to that inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart in the right way, if you have sewn the head of the siphac or coustit or where you have sewn with the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make him pierce from another part of the inner section up to the point of failure;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this treatment is that you sew them thus as the tanner makes the skins,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the seam of one part, and retake from another, until the treatment is fully accomplished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of treatment, which Galen describes properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	it is thus like any spring, which naturally assemble the injured parts together.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one head to the other head, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	fix a needle or a head of a mirror close by, and make it pierce the limb slightly.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the injured heads come together;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce through the weak part just up to the inner core.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as it is the head of the deep wound;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make a piercing on one and the other side of the weak part just up to the inner core, in other heads of the deep wound that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Here are the translations:
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must cauterize the belly with .ij. needles, or have thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew up wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is a more grievous wound than others in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound in all its blood, thus it seems the artery has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you reset the intestine, and the cut; then put on the powder soothing flesh,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and it seems the artery has moved, if you put on no ointment that is present, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and they pull the thread, and are sewn the suture, and the mirror;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with others, until it be healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, put them on, as soon as it begins to gather pus, much cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and remove it twice a day until it be healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you do not have another kind of medicine for many types of simple wounds.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will not affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary that you moisten a light linen cloth with oil of temperate warmth, or with rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it between the joints, and beneath the soles;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or pruritus in his belly, and often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they clysterize with red wine immediately, and meanwhile the pruritus reaches up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it penetrates within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is by the plaintiveness of the veins that they are, and by the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach to their natural disposition.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the stitching bursts from the wound, set it back together as in the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turns towards green or black, then you must lay the black place that corrodes the blood which comes from it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the nail
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the eyes facing the part below the wound until it befits to alleviate the extraction when the wounds heal, and the wounds close.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the swelling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is wounded, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one cannot restore it to some joints,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a spear or a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and it was a wound on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and thus caused the evacuation and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I go to cure according to what I can do, and did not cease from subtle treatment until he was healthy, and the eyes were sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sound, I doubted that the patient had no evil in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no point of evil, but he remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take firm hold of large clamps, then assemble the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the clamp has opened its mouth, then place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if it stretches its mouth open;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then the scalp is cut, and this holds so that it cannot be dislocated,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then apply another fringe afterwards in the same way as before, so that the wound is entirely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head becomes stuck in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is taken from the intestine of a beast,
en teil maniere:	in such manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestine filament that is very loose,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then attach it to the head of this subtle twisted thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reset it in its proper position;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of cauterizing of frenzy is not otherwise than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and large, especially when it is in one of the intestinal passages, if there is no ingenious remedy, unless subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and similarly when it is shaved and made numb.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the true notation of a hard and white abscess, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also shaved like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it appears clear and numb, and other times dense;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes a little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healthy, and there is no flesh;
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is not outside one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, by the small loss of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	for his wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	for because he has hard skin within, and on the lips, which does not allow any flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the pus is stagnant, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because for that reason the corruption is a kind of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where by the property in the region it is slow digestion, and slow health, and naturally inflamed;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicine in this section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is fitting that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula which is done by surgical operation with hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	where at the spleen, or at the intestine, or at the bladder, or at some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or at the spine of the back, or at some joint of the hands or of the feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens that it comes to the ownership of the main limb, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is no remedy but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is an ulcer that does not heal until it reaches the place I have described, and you are confident in your treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you examine it carefully, if you take a thread of iron or copper, the ulcer is straight, if it is circular;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the ulcer is twisted, seek it out with a subtle thread of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the leads bend back into the twist;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and you should make a fistula at badly perforated places and you cannot search well by feeling.
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you touch it with one of the perforations,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one perforation to another, and it suppurates;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should examine it with your power, so that you recognize if there is bone or nerve, and it is separated by the fontanelle;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and the place where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, if the treatment is according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the decayed and rotten flesh that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healthy
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well perforated in the right place, it is necessary that you cut open deeply, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I apply gentle poultices in medicine agar, and the buds just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity which is remaining at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he puts ointments on his wounds, as long as they are healing;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healing through this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut around it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve is not causing grief to principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if his skin is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, so let it be treated until the decay is completely removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the things that are wounded so much that they become healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and rents a gap as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not at the same level as just now:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you discover and seek as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot come to an end;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if it has a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with bandages,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is done with a suitable instrument for that,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, so extract them all, do not leave even one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes you counter, there is no error or fear
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it grips and moistens and fleshes, and releases the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot dislodge them for an hour, then put on the wound a poultice causing purification,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the pus is purified between the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have lighter bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as of the thigh or shin,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove so much of the corrupted flesh that the blackness is entirely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the body corrupted, it comes just below the bone of the shoulder;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to open and cut just up to the corruption, and then to treat until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take an example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	It was a young man of around 30 years, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the materials came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and had no way to evacuate by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physician, in their foolishness, operated so much that they opened up the abscesses,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in corroding many materials, and it became fistulous, and there were many perforations that all gnawed away the moisture of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many times I mirrored the cure within ten years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they cured it,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which corrodes through the perforations in a large body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I thrust a tent into one of these perforations, and then I searched all the perforations.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some veins come against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut into one of the perforations as far as I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came right up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I watched what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, because it is what I saw.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and discovered the bone as it was beforehand,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and I watched it, and then I examined it, and I thought of healing the limb;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I do not touch it as much as I grasp around a palm of the bone, and I make the trajectory right on its whole.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines; and he was quickly healed and freed suddenly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it is not necessary to restart the work forcibly because of the weakness of the patient, who cannot bear it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For because of the evacuation of blood it often happens, but it was completely healthy,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard lump formed in the bone, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction in anything, neither in going nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take the ligament, and stretch it to the head of the bone which opens,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command him to extend it high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another bandage of a larger size than the first one, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head, so that you draw out the corrupted flesh from underneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the bone where you see the sore, so that the sore does not spread to the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a thin layer of cotton or a tablet under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to probe thus in order to see and feel the corruption, and to probe again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the entire flesh; then put a thin layer of cotton underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then the decay spreads from one part to another, and is the decay of the length of the corruption, a small piece, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the decay is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and let the bone or what it contains be from another part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the decay is in the continuity of the joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut off;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the decay is in the hand or foot, it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but you must inquire into this corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and examine it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not contradict you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the veins are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the outlets,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare each similar appearance of work with his instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will have mastery of, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and it bears witness to the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument which you have mastery of, according to what it needs.
dou feu	for fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head collapses either because of a cause inside or because of a fever.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have applied the medicine to that corroded place through the treatment with medicines, and it does not improve at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should amputate that limb up to the level where the corrosion comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	If the patient is weakened by fear of death, or by spite, which is greater, from the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness spreads, then it corrodes one limb after another,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; if you hasten to cope with it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and it is through the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar things,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	the corrosion is at the finger joint, thus the cope, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, thus the cope at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, thus the cope at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there are no better remedies than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and you should do it in this way when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then it takes hold after another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, it takes hold of the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then it takes hold at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and it comes above the knee, if there is no other remedy than to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to cope or to soothe the limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister below one of the ligatures, and another minister above the other ligature,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you separate the flesh that is between the two ligatures at a spacious interval, so that the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then take the cup or basin, and place a piece of linen, so that the thread does not touch the healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and let it come to the patient for another wound and abscess ulceration.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood flows out when you operate, then cauterize the skin hastily,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	where you apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then let the numb member recover with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will count as one who had a similar wound:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a black spot that seemed to be burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first into his finger through the wound, so that it took over the entire finger;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man sees the decay, if he hastens to cover the foot, and was healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and soon after, the decay returned in his hand, or in the other, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied things that rebounded after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he saw that I covered his hand, and I did not want, that I had hoped to recover the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubt also that if he cuts off his hand, it will not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was feeble; and he despaired totally, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he ceased to coop up his hand, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not known any account of those who were better than what one does elsewhere, so that one has mastery.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does a abscess come to a head swollen with charcoal, and stays for so long that it makes a large collection of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus jumps out, and clears the eyes' sight, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as subtle as the delicate sheets of a cloak,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not corrode nor just to the bone, nor just to the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called “fistula”;
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but since it is so prolonged that it reaches just to the bone in the front, then it is called “fistula”;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so thin that you can see the entire course of the vein, and similarly when it is subtle, just like a delicate sheet;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not differ due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you find that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not on the surface,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, if the treatment of the cluster thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look at the sinews which are large, and the abscess that comes from them is of foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then the clustering of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Here is the translation:
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	as long as the medicine is red, and it becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take some of it according to your need, and make it into a thin liquid and into honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and cleanse the wound with it, and hold the opening steady;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay on for two hours, then wipe it off in a sprinkling manner;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times, until the breast is exhausted, and the pus is eliminated.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and none of those times is it cleansed with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes from the wood of vines, and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it, and cleanse with it, until you know that the breast is well purified;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot suffer it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash of cinders
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if they purify with water and honey or have a little bit of litargyre crushed;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	where you purify with honey and wine mixed, so that the honey has the property of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the healthy ones strong;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the senses are well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if you cleanse what makes the flesh grow in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take a definitive plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you cleanse with certain medications and ointments, whose properties I have described in the treatise on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the perforation of the breast is small, and the cane of the lancet cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you widen it with a iron a little, and put in a tent of the Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or ointment of balsam, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then cut and leave it so slightly that the cane of the lancet can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if you pierce where the swelling is above, whether it gathers here or lower than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the swelling is in depth, do not let it grow again there;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut beneath the skin thus as you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	it appears in such a way that the swelling runs to the lowest place it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bowel is perforated, if he does not let it suppurate therein
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the seat below as if you saw,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	it appears in such a manner: that the bowel runs more lightly downwards, and leaves nothing of the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the seat,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stand on the drapery of the loin that covers the whole back;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then gather all the strength in the right place of the back, i.e. a little larger than at first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then there is a gentle pressure on the other drapery according to the quantity of the back,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the back of the back to align the bowl, and do not remove the large drapery unless after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is above the pertussis of the breast, often opens by opening the mouth,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows that which runs from the mouth, whether it is venom or little or enough, or digests, or does not digest;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed of the patient's sensation of pain or name, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been extended in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps above the pertussis of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	Here is the translation:
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then dislocate it in the morning, or the third day, and when you dislocate the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if it changes, I will use another dressing, and renew the binding.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the senses are troubled with indigestion after many days, know that the senses are not yet clear.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if you feel subtle pains in the short term after long tension, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because health is approaching. Because there are men who delay the healing of their wounds, and those that do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the bowel is indigestible, it knows how to overcome the pain after many days, it knows that the breasts do not stray;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts delay healing, and are sluggish, then apply medicines which are moist in substance and dry in virtue;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as we have mentioned before, because there is a great part of vitriol, and it is the last resort medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a treatment of yaufinite, and they make it with rose oil, and the extract of old wine in equal substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then they confit and use it; and this same mixture makes cooked honey thickened,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when yaufinite treatment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glues .I. a bandage, and he stops it over the breast, and sometimes he administers to an Aristologist a long time,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the sky-blue, which is as if flour of times and hundred;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in use of simples or of compounds: crush them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and in use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and it is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then you know that corruption is deep-seated, and it makes an impression on the bone, where the hard limbs are, or the sinews;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if you treat a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that grows beneath the finger nail, near the joint of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	where you tread, or where by chance you are born with other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is inflamed, and one does not take care, if an abscess comes to the heel,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and throw so much that they run over the root of the ankle, and by chance they run it entirely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there come the ulcers just to the bone, so that they bring painful hurt, and it is the head of the wide toe, and its color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat them as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluous flesh which remains on the finger,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterizations are great help if the bones are sound, and the finger is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if he has an ulcer on his skin, and it begins to point, and the blister,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	it is necessary that you put the right remedy under the ulcer that points to the skin,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and apply pressure from above, and touch the subtle and delicate skin,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining skin medicine burning and corrosive to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of wounds until they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut into it, and extract fiercely, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the decayed tooth, then cut into it, in the same way as it was said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and swollen, and he feels great pain, then you must soothe it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the thorn-like growth that has grown in a crosswise direction across,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the cutting does not touch the flesh which is beneath the thorn-like growth, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it has happened, then put something on it to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain which comes from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two fingers that are born in the hands of certain men by chance are completely numb,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance they have a piece or a bone, and sometimes they have a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in none of us two fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those who are born with a defect of their finger do not move it,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those who are born at the joint of their finger, perhaps move by chance;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of one who is withered is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Here is the translation:
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or has a hernia in the back, it is necessary that you first take hold of the round flesh just up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then take hold of the bone at a suitable angle for that, then cure until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come in two ways come from birth, or from sudden injury, or from burning by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you take hold of the dislocation, and that the bone is reset according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two warm tents or oil-soaked cloths, so they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two subtle pieces of lead, as long as the joint is stuck, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	They stick to one of these two with the palm, if you apply that sticking as it is necessary.
Des vils	Of veins
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	You see gross swollen veins full of superfluous melancholic humors that come into many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they especially occur in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry heavy loads, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary therefore that you administer sometimes a purging of the colon, and then the sap of the basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron is according to two methods: one is that they are burned, and another treats the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another way is to open the vein, and to pull out entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is done in this manner: raise the first leg of hot water very strongly, so that the large veins are made subtle.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg of the patient down from the hip just to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut into the vein in one place, or in two, or in three, with a large incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then he releases and draws the black blood from his hand, from one vein to the other, until as much blood flows out as the virtues of the disease can suffer.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then he lies down, and orders that he be fed on rich game and black coal;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommend the evacuation and the bloodletting when the veins are full, and annoy the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevations of it are according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then put him in a bath, and let the swollen leg be cooled down until it turns red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it with fire, and then cover the vein from the loin to the knee, or in the part below the joint;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the ankle, and scratch the vein of that part, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems as if a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then apply the remedy underneath, so it lifts the skin from the raw flesh, and then place it on the lighter side of the wound.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cover it in another layer above, with two inches; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then leave it to settle, as you have done, and place it on another ulcer, as you did previously;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cover with another dressing, or more if you have mastery of it, then leave it, and cover the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Here is the translation:
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it back and lift it, then he will stick a needle everywhere, fully, to double the thread strongly.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and pull and pull, and he will stick below, he will sew, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it holds.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and beware that it does not swell, for if it swells, one cannot pull or lift, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have fully pulled it back, then put on the wound a dressing of millet flour in wine and rose oil; and treat until he is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if his sight is constricted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said.
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that you bend it straight, but do not cover it yet; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron that one uses to cover the sight is curved, and does not cut, so it does not touch the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of large curvature, for if it were subtle, it would touch the vein, but it is thick as we have said, and this is the shape.
De la voinne civile	About civil veins
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is in the legs, in hot and dry regions where no herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps grows elsewhere besides the legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that lies beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes from within the body, snakes and worms, growing between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes into the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then it changes the veins, and begins to make the vein issue forth, like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is open, it is necessary that you envelop it with a piece of cloth from one and a half inches to the nail, and the neck,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the cloth remain on the leg, and all the times it does not fall off, if you envelop it around the cloth, and the nail;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it is fully exposed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess and putridity or ulceration, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because it is necessary that it be treated little by little just to the head, and nothing remains there or in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and it is not often that this vein is treated with five or ten pounds of longitude, or of X.;
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one hand comes to me, on which it is seated from ten palms in length, and when you take hold of it, if you prick or pierce, and it perforates just to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	Here is the translation:
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And often at this vein many times, and similarly when it opens in the joint of the foot, or where the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes from many perforations, and where it jumps many times; cure the wounds thus as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cow's disease", because it often affects cows.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the whole body, ascending and descending,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it feels like a good sensation when going from member to member, until it reaches the skin or where it goes, and it bursts forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is generated by putridity of certain humors, as if they come from worms and snakes and lice and ascarids or the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its evil, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance returns, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you want to cure and treat, if one cannot do more than when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	it is necessary then that you read the place above and below with a strong and well-tightened ligature,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and the tract further, and if the vein is deeply in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If you cauterize with fire above, as long as it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that he does, if it is that he runs to the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or approaching near the eye, hold your eyebrow firmly in place, then cut above, and remove it completely;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is suitable to use the patient's purification of bodily medications through dissolving medicines for bad humors,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of rotten meat causing putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I see what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it swell up like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more painful than anything, as if living silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place, and fixed itself in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little after, it corrects throughout the whole body, so much that it comes into the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then it returns again to the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease according to this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many that had wanted to move the pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not understand what he wants, as I saw it in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, it seems that the constrained wind appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and I did not appear to follow this reason for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and recovered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you want to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, it reveals itself as we have said.
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the disease lingers above and below hastily, and then presses upon it until that windiness constrains it to its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you treat those who expel windiness, as with foul pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Arrows.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they stick.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and notched ones, and smooth ones;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those which have sharp angles, and those which have length, and those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls onto a member if it falls according to seven ways: or into a principal member it divides,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore into a place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you about afterwards, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then it is necessary that you take care of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in more severe conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad symptom does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply implanted, if it pulls, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the symptom of the brain when the arrow head lies there and pierces the bone, and removes the swelling which is on the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	it is when there is dimness and swooning and vertigo in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and perversion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without strength in the nostrils, or in the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and it jumps from the white moist wound resembling a poultice, and it jumps also as if bruised flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this is a sign that appears, if you hold back from the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not inside.
